Integrate basic visibility and usage within the existing Blazor WebAssembly app.\n\n## Target Users\n- Internal engineers and product owners modeling engine builds.\n- Future UI users who will configure engine builds and see completion status.\n- Developers and testers extending the data model and completion logic.\n\n## Key Outcomes\n- A coherent relational schema that:\n  - Represents engine families with variable rotor counts.\n  - Represents part categories, hierarchical category trees, and relationships.\n  - Represents parts, kits (via BOM-style components), and vendor offerings.\n  - Represents user builds and build selections.\n- A completion query that:\n  - Computes required quantities per category using formula rules.\n  - Expands kits via BOM into underlying parts.\n  - Aggregates supplied quantities per category (including expanded kits).\n  - Compares required vs supplied and returns status/progress.\n\n## Scope & Features\n\n### Schema & Migrations\nDeliver a MySQL-compatible schema migration at `db/migrations/001_init.sql` that includes tables (with appropriate PKs, FKs, indexes, and common metadata where useful):\n\n- Category\n- CategoryTree\n- CategoryEdge\n- EngineFamily\n- CategoryRequirement\n- Part\n- PartCategory\n- PartComponent (for kit/BOM expansion)\n- Vendor\n- PartOffering\n- Build\n- BuildSelection\n\nKey behaviors:\n- Support multiple category trees (e.g., `"core"`).\n- Support parent/child relationships via CategoryEdge for hierarchical queries.\n- CategoryRequirement:\n  - Links an EngineFamily and Category to a formula defining required quantity.\n  - Formula must support expressions such as `3 * rotor_count`.\n- PartComponent:\n  - Supports kits by defining component parts and quantities.\n- Build & BuildSelection:\n  - Link an EngineFamily to a user build.\n  - Track which parts (and quantities) are selected for a build.\n\n### Seed Data\nDeliver a minimal but rich dataset in `db/seeds/seed_minimal.sql`:\n\n- EngineFamily:\n  - At least one: `13B-REW` with `rotor_count = 2`.\n- Category & Trees:\n  - At least one tree named `"core"`.\n  - Categories including: `apex seals`, `side seals`, `coolant seals`, and several others.\n- CategoryRequirement:\n  - At least one formula rule using `rotor_count`, e.g.:\n    - Apex seals: `3 * rotor_count`.\n  - Enough additional rules to test multiple categories and edge cases.\n- Parts:\n  - At least 30 parts distributed across categories.\n- Kits:\n  - Integrate basic visibility and usage within the existing Blazor WebAssembly app.\n\n## Target Users\n- Internal engineers and product owners modeling engine builds.\n- Future UI users who will configure engine builds and see completion status.\n- Developers and testers extending the data model and completion logic.\n\n## Key Outcomes\n- A coherent relational schema that:\n  - Links an EngineFamily and Category to a formula defining required quantity.\n  - Formula must support expressions such as `3 * rotor_count`.\n- PartComponent:\n  - Supports kits by defining component parts and quantities.\n- Build & BuildSelection:\n  - At least one formula rule using `rotor_count`, e.g.:\n    - Apex seals: `3 * rotor_count`.\n  - Enough additional rules to test multiple categories and edge cases.\n- Parts:\n  - At least 30 parts distributed across categories.\n- Kits:\n  - At least one example build referencing `13B-REW` with selected parts/kits to validate completion logic.\n\n### Completion Query\n- Implement one or more SQL queries (or views) that:\n  - Compute required quantity per category:\n    - Uses EngineFamily attributes (rotor_count) plus CategoryRequirement formulas.\n  - Compute supplied quantity per category:\n    - Expands kits via PartComponent so supplied quantity includes underlying components.\n    - Aggregates over BuildSelection for a specific build.\n  - Compare required vs supplied and project:\n    - Per-category fields such as:\n      - `category_id`, `category_name`\n      - `required_quantity`\n      - `supplied_quantity`\n      - `status` (e.g., COMPLETE / INCOMPLETE / OVERFULFILLED)\n      - `progress` (e.g., `supplied / required`, capped at 1.0).\n- Ensure at least one testable query exists that clearly demonstrates the apex seal requirement using `3 * rotor_count` for `13B-REW`.\n\n### Documentation\n- `docs/DATA_MODEL.md`:\n  - Update with full table list.\n  - For each table: columns (name, type, purpose), primary keys, and key relationships.\n  - Mention how kits and category requirements are represented.\n- Root `README.md`:\n  - Instructions to set up MySQL, run migrations/seeds, and run the Blazor app locally.\n  - Clear steps to:\n    - Configure DB connection for the Blazor app.\n    - Execute completion query for a sample build.\n    - Run any provided tests.\n- `logs/CHANGELOG.md`:\n  - Add a concise summary line describing this EPIC 01 schema work and test coverage added.\n\n### Blazor Integration\n- Work strictly in the existing `app/` folder for application code.\n  - Do not create `frontend/` or `backend/` folders.\n- Update:\n  - `app/Program.cs` for DB connection configuration and any service registration required to query the database (e.g., HTTP API proxy or direct API client as appropriate to the project’s existing patterns).\n  - `app/Pages/*` with at least one page that:\n    - Shows a build’s completion status.\n    - Displays category-level required vs supplied quantities and status for a sample build.\n  - `app/wwwroot/*` as needed (e.g., basic styles or assets for data visualization).\n- Provide clear instructions to run the Blazor app locally:\n  - Include `dotnet run` from the `app/` directory.\n  - Any environment variables or configuration required for DB connectivity.\n\n## Constraints & Non-Goals\n- Use MySQL-compatible SQL syntax (no vendor-specific features from other DBs).\n- The focus is on schema and queries, not advanced UI/UX.\n- Do not introduce new top-level folders such as `frontend/` or `backend/`.\n- Keep logic that belongs to the DB in SQL; only minimal C#/Blazor is required to:\n  - Demonstrate the completion query results.\n  - Prove the apex seal requirement works end-to-end.\n\n---\n\nAGENT_TASKS.md:\n# AGENT_TASKS – EPIC 01: Data Foundation\n\n## Designer\n\n**Project Name:** EPIC 01 – Data Foundation\n\n**Required Deliverables:**\n- `docs/DATA_MODEL.md`\n  - Purpose: Compute per-category required vs supplied quantities and status for a given build.\n- Updates to `app/Program.cs` and any supporting code (if backend access is proxied through a service layer in the Blazor app)\n  - Purpose: Ensure the Blazor app can retrieve completion data from the database or API.\n\n**Key Technical Notes & Constraints:**\n- Use MySQL-compatible SQL syntax.\n- Schema requirements:\n  - Tables:\n    - `Category`: master list of categories (e.g., apex seals).\n    - `CategoryTree`: named trees (e.g., `"core"`).\n    - `CategoryEdge`: parent-child edges for category hierarchies.\n    - `EngineFamily`: includes rotor count and identifier (`13B-REW`).\n    - `CategoryRequirement`: links engine families and categories to quantity formulas.\n    - `Part`: all individual parts and kits.\n    - `PartCategory`: mapping between parts and categories.\n    - `PartComponent`: BOM table to define kit components and quantities.\n    - `Vendor`: part suppliers.\n    - `PartOffering`: offerings/prices per vendor and part.\n    - `Build`: user/engine builds, linked to engine families.\n    - `BuildSelection`: parts (and quantities) selected for a build.\n  - Ensure foreign keys reflect these relationships and support seeding order.\n- Seed data requirements:\n  - `EngineFamily`:\n    - Insert `13B-REW` with `rotor_count = 2`.\n  - Categories:\n    - Include at least apex seals, side seals, coolant seals, and additional categories.\n  - Requirements:\n    - Encode formula rules such as `3 * rotor_count` for apex seals.\n    - Design formula storage so it can be evaluated or interpreted (SQL expression string, operator/operand fields, or similar).\n  - Parts:\n    - At least 30 parts across categories.\n  - Kits/BOM:\n    - At least 2 kits defined via `PartComponent` that expand into multiple components.\n  - Vendor/Offering:\n    - At least one vendor and multiple `PartOffering` entries.\n  - Builds:\n    - At least one build for `13B-REW` with selections that demonstrate both complete and incomplete categories.\n- Completion query:\n  - Must:\n    - Calculate `required_quantity` per category from `CategoryRequirement` and `EngineFamily` attributes.\n    - Aggregate `supplied_quantity` per category from `BuildSelection`, expanding kits via `PartComponent` and respecting quantities.\n    - Output per category:\n      - `category_id`, `category_name`\n      - `required_quantity`\n      - `supplied_quantity`\n      - `status` (e.g., via CASE expression).\n      - `progress` (e.g., `LEAST(1.0, supplied_quantity / required_quantity)`).\n  - Demonstrate that for `13B-REW` and apex seals, requirement equals `3 * 2 = 6`.\n- Integration:\n  - Expose a way for the Blazor app to access completion data:\n    - Either via an existing backend/API contract or, if this is a standalone data layer exercise, via a mock or static JSON load for now (align with existing architecture).\n  - Update `app/Program.cs` accordingly if any new services or clients are required.\n- No new folders `frontend/` or `backend/` may be created.\n\n---\n\n## Tester\n\n**Project Name:** EPIC 01 – Data Foundation\n\n**Required Deliverables:**\n- Test execution notes (location consistent with project practice; can reference this `TEST.md`)\n  - High-Level UX Goals\n\n- Make the data model and completion logic understandable to developers at a glance.\n- Provide a simple, reliable way to:\n  - Run the Blazor app locally.\n  - See a build’s completion status by category.\n  - Map what’s shown in the UI back to the schema and completion query.\n- Favor clarity and low cognitive load over visual polish:\n  - Text-first layout.\n  - Simple table-based presentation.\n  - Minimal but meaningful color usage.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Primary User Flows\n\n### 2.1 Developer: Setup & Run\n\n1. Open project root.\n2. Read `README.md`:\n   - See prerequisites (MySQL, .NET SDK).\n   - Copy/paste commands to:\n     1. Create DB.\n     2. Apply migration.\n     3. Apply seed.\n   - See a clearly marked “Run the Blazor app” section.\n3. Run `cd app && dotnet run`.\n4. Open browser at provided URL (e.g., `https://localhost:5001`).\n5. Navigate to the build completion page via:\n   - Main nav link like “Build Completion”.\n   - Or default/home page link/button.\n\nOutcome: Developer sees a table of categories with required vs supplied quantities and status.\n\n### 2.2 Developer: Understand Data Model\n\n1. Open `docs/DATA_MODEL.md`.\n2. Scan top-level overview diagram/description of core entities:\n   - EngineFamily, Category, CategoryTree, CategoryEdge, CategoryRequirement.\n   - Part, PartCategory, PartComponent.\n   - Vendor, PartOffering.\n   - Build, BuildSelection.\n3. For each table, see a standard section:\n   - Purpose (1–2 sentences).\n   - Columns table (name, type, nullable, purpose).\n   - Keys & relationships (FKs, notable indexes).\n4. See a dedicated subsection:\n   - “Category Requirements & Formulas”.\n   - “Kits & Part Components (BOM-style)”.\n   - “Completion Query Overview” (high-level logic summary).\n\nOutcome: Developer can mentally map DB tables to the UI and logic.\n\n### 2.3 Tester: Verify Completion Logic\n\n1. Follow `README.md` steps to set up DB and app.\n2. Execute completion query (SQL snippet included in README or `DATA_MODEL.md`).\n3. Run the Blazor app and open build completion page.\n4. Compare:\n   - Apex seal requirement (6 for 13B-REW with `rotor_count = 2`).\n   - Required/supplied for a few other categories.\n5. Log observations in test notes; confirm acceptance criteria.\n\nOutcome: Tester can confirm end-to-end behavior without guessing.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Blazor UI Design – Build Completion Page\n\n### 3.1 Page Identity\n\n- **File**: `app/Pages/BuildCompletion.razor` (name can vary but conceptually this page).\n- **Route**: `/build-completion/{buildId:int?}`\n  - If `buildId` is not supplied:\n    - Use a default example build ID from seed data (documented in README).\n    - Show a hint: “Showing example build #X from seed data.”\n  - If `buildId` is supplied:\n    - Load completion data for that build.\n    - Show build identifier and engine family at top if available.\n\n### 3.2 Layout Structure\n\n1. **Page Header**\n   - Title: “Build Completion Status”\n   - Subtitle/description line:\n     - “Per-category required vs supplied quantities for a rotary engine build.”\n   - Build info block:\n     - `Build: <build_name or ID>`\n     - `Engine Family: 13B-REW (rotor_count = 2)` (or dynamic)\n     - A small note if using seeded example.\n\n2. **Build Selector (Optional but Recommended)**\n   - Simple text input or dropdown for build ID:\n     - Label: “Build ID”\n     - Input: numeric (or dropdown if convenient).\n     - Button: “Load Build” triggers reload.\n   - Keep minimal; failure to load should show a clear error (see 3.4).\n\n3. **Summary Status Panel**\n   - At top, small panel with:\n     - Overall status: derived from categories (e.g., COMPLETE only if all categories complete or overfulfilled).\n     - Overall progress: maybe simple text like:\n       - “Complete Categories: 4 / 7”\n       - “Incomplete Categories: 3 / 7”\n     - Optional simple progress bar:\n       - Filled percentage = complete_categories / total_categories.\n   - Colors:\n     - If all categories COMPLETE or OVERFULFILLED: green label “COMPLETE”.\n     - Otherwise: amber label “IN PROGRESS” (or red if mostly incomplete).\n\n4. **Category Table**\n\n   Central content as a table with columns:\n\n   - **Category**\n     - Category name (e.g., “Apex Seals”, “Side Seals”).\n   - **Required Qty**\n   - **Supplied Qty**\n   - **Status**\n     - Text values: `COMPLETE`, `INCOMPLETE`, `OVERFULFILLED`, optionally `NOT REQUIRED` if required_quantity is 0.\n     - Status cell visually distinguished by color:\n       - COMPLETE: green text or badge.\n       - INCOMPLETE: red text or badge.\n       - OVERFULFILLED: blue or purple text/badge.\n   - **Progress**\n     - Display as:\n       - Ratio: `supplied / required` (e.g., `4 / 6`) when required > 0.\n       - And/or percentage: `66%`.\n       - When required = 0:\n         - Show “N/A” or “–”.\n     - Optionally a simple, narrow bar showing fill proportion.\n\n   Row ordering:\n   - Default: group by status (INCOMPLETE first), or simply sort by Category name alphabetically.\n   - For simplicity: sort alphabetically by category name.\n\n5. **Legend / Notes**\n\n   At bottom/right-side small text:\n\n   - “COMPLETE: supplied quantity equals required quantity.”\n   - “INCOMPLETE: supplied quantity is less than required quantity.”\n   - “OVERFULFILLED: supplied quantity is greater than required quantity.”\n   - “Progress is capped at 100% (1.0).”\n\n   Add an explicit note about kits:\n\n   - “Note: Kits selected in the build are expanded into their component parts when computing supplied quantities.”\n\n### 3.3 Loading, Empty, and Error States\n\n- **Loading State**\n  - When data is being fetched:\n    - Replace table body with a row showing “Loading build completion data…”.\n    - Or show a centered text spinner placeholder (plain text is acceptable).\n\n- **Error State**\n  - If data fetch fails (e.g., HTTP error or parse error):\n    - Show an inline error banner above the table:\n      - Red/amber background, border, or text.\n      - Message: “Unable to load completion data for build #X. Please check the backend/API configuration or try again.”\n    - Allow retry via:\n      - “Retry” button next to the build ID input, or refresh the page.\n\n- **Empty State**\n  - If no categories are returned (unusual):\n    - Show: “No completion data available for this build. Ensure the build exists and has associated category requirements.”\n\n### 3.4 Responsiveness & Accessibility\n\n- Table should:\n  - Collapse horizontally on smaller screens by:\n    - Allowing horizontal scroll.\n  - Keep font sizes legible; no heavy reflow required.\n- Status colors must be distinguishable even for color-blind users:\n  - Use icons or text labels in addition to color:\n    - COMPLETE: “● COMPLETE” (green dot).\n    - INCOMPLETE: “● INCOMPLETE” (red dot).\n    - OVERFULFILLED: “● OVERFULFILLED” (blue dot).\n- Use semantic HTML where possible:\n  - `<table>`, `<thead>`, `<tbody>`, `<th>`, `<tr>`, `<td>` etc.\n  - Descriptive heading `<h1>`, `<h2>`.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Define `PartComponent` semantics:\n     - `parent_part` is the kit.\n     - `component_part` is a part contained within the kit.\n     - `quantity` indicates how many of that component.\n   - Explain how kits expand in the completion query.\n\n7. **Completion Query Overview**\n   - Step 3: Map parts to categories via `PartCategory`.\n     - Step 4: Aggregate supplied quantities per category.\n     - Step 5: Join required & supplied, compute:\n       - `status` with CASE.\n       - Integrate basic visibility and usage within the existing Blazor WebAssembly app.\n\n## Target Users\n- Internal engineers and product owners modeling engine builds.\n- Future UI users who will configure engine builds and see completion status.\n- Developers and testers extending the data model and completion logic.\n\n## Key Outcomes\n- A coherent relational schema that:\n  - Represents engine families with variable rotor counts.\n  - Represents part categories, hierarchical category trees, and relationships.\n  - Represents parts, kits (via BOM-style components), and vendor offerings.\n  - Represents user builds and build selections.\n- A completion query that:\n  - Computes required quantities per category using formula rules.\n  - Expands kits via BOM into underlying parts.\n  - Aggregates supplied quantities per category (including expanded kits).\n  - Compares required vs supplied and returns status/progress.\n\n## Scope & Features\n\n### Schema & Migrations\nDeliver a MySQL-compatible schema migration at `db/migrations/001_init.sql` that includes tables (with appropriate PKs, FKs, indexes, and common metadata where useful):\n\n- Category\n- CategoryTree\n- CategoryEdge\n- EngineFamily\n- CategoryRequirement\n- Part\n- PartCategory\n- PartComponent (for kit/BOM expansion)\n- Vendor\n- PartOffering\n- Build\n- BuildSelection\n\nKey behaviors:\n- Support multiple category trees (e.g., `"core"`).\n- Support parent/child relationships via CategoryEdge for hierarchical queries.\n- CategoryRequirement:\n  - Links an EngineFamily and Category to a formula defining required quantity.\n  - Formula must support expressions such as `3 * rotor_count`.\n- PartComponent:\n  - Supports kits by defining component parts and quantities.\n- Build & BuildSelection:\n  - Link an EngineFamily to a user build.\n  - Track which parts (and quantities) are selected for a build.\n\n### Seed Data\nDeliver a minimal but rich dataset in `db/seeds/seed_minimal.sql`:\n\n- EngineFamily:\n  - At least one: `13B-REW` with `rotor_count = 2`.\n- Category & Trees:\n  - At least one tree named `"core"`.\n  - Categories including: `apex seals`, `side seals`, `coolant seals`, and several others.\n- CategoryRequirement:\n  - `Category`: master list of categories (e.g., apex seals).\n    - `CategoryTree`: named trees (e.g., `"core"`).\n    - `CategoryEdge`: parent-child edges for category hierarchies.\n    - `EngineFamily`: includes rotor count and identifier (`13B-REW`).\n    - `CategoryRequirement`: links engine families and categories to quantity formulas.\n    - `Part`: all individual parts and kits.\n    - `PartCategory`: mapping between parts and categories.\n    - `PartComponent`: BOM table to define kit components and quantities.\n    - `Vendor`: part suppliers.\n    - `PartOffering`: offerings/prices per vendor and part.\n    - `Build`: user/engine builds, linked to engine families.\n    - `BuildSelection`: parts (and quantities) selected for a build.\n  - Builds:\n    - At least one build for `13B-REW` with selections that demonstrate both complete and incomplete categories.\n- Completion query:\n  - Must:\n    - Calculate `required_quantity` per category from `CategoryRequirement` and `EngineFamily` attributes.\n    - `required_quantity`\n      - `supplied_quantity`\n      - `status` (e.g., via CASE expression).\n      - `progress` (e.g., `LEAST(1.0, supplied_quantity / required_quantity)`).\n  - Demonstrate that for `13B-REW` and apex seals, requirement equals `3 * 2 = 6`.\n- Integration:\n  - Expose a way for the Blazor app to access completion data:\n    - Either via an existing backend/API contract or, if this is a standalone data layer exercise, via a mock or static JSON load for now (align with existing architecture).\n  - Update `app/Program.cs` accordingly if any new services or clients are required.\n- No new folders `frontend/` or `backend/` may be created.\n\n---\n\n## Tester\n\n**Project Name:** EPIC 01 – Data Foundation\n\n**Required Deliverables:**\n- Test execution notes (location consistent with project practice; can reference this `TEST.md`)\n  - Migrations & Schema\n\n### 1.1 Base Schema Created\n- [Owner] Backend  \n**Task:** Verify `db/migrations/001_init.sql` creates all required tables with correct structure.\n\n**Acceptance Criteria:**\n- Running `001_init.sql` on a clean MySQL database succeeds without errors.\n- Tables exist: `Category`, `CategoryTree`, `CategoryEdge`, `EngineFamily`, `CategoryRequirement`, `Part`, `PartCategory`, `PartComponent`, `Vendor`, `PartOffering`, `Build`, `BuildSelection`.\n- Each table has:\n  - A primary key.\n  - Necessary foreign keys (e.g., `CategoryRequirement.engine_family_id -> EngineFamily`, `PartCategory.part_id -> Part`, `Build.engine_family_id -> EngineFamily`, `PartComponent.parent_part_id -> Part`, etc.).\n- Schema uses appropriate data types (e.g., integer for counts, decimal for prices, varchar for names).\n- No FK cycles that prevent seeding in a straightforward order.\n\n### 1.2 Category Tree Integrity\n- [Owner] Backend  \n**Task:** Validate the category tree structure.\n\n**Acceptance Criteria:**\n- `CategoryTree` can store at least the `"core"` tree.\n- `CategoryEdge` correctly links parent and child categories.\n- Inserting sample categories with edges does not violate constraints.\n- Querying edges for `"core"` returns a coherent tree (no orphaned nodes if not intended).\n\n## 2. Builder Page: `/builder/{buildId}`\nMain layout:\n- Left rail: CategoryTree\n  - Shows 10 categories in a tree or flat list (static seeded list acceptable).\n  - Selecting a category updates the center panel.\n- Center panel: PartsList\n  - Lists parts for the selected category from static JSON.\n  - Allows selecting/deselecting parts.\n- Right rail: SummaryRail + WarningsPanel\n  - Displays:\n    - Completion percentage (selected vs required parts).\n    - Total build cost (sum of selected part prices).\n    - Warnings list (static examples OK, but must respond to write actions data).\n\n### 3. Accepts selection changes for parts (e.g., add/update).\n  - Recomputes completion, cost, warnings.\n  - Returns `{ summary, completion, cost, warnings }`.\n- `DELETE /api/builds/:id/selections`\n  - Accepts info to remove/reset selections.\n  - Recomputes metrics.\n  - Returns `{ summary, completion, cost, warnings }`.\n\n## Non-Functional Requirements\n- Local development:\n  - Clear instructions in root `README.md` for:\n    - Use standard Blazor routing to map `/builder/{buildId}` to `BuilderPage`.\n  - Use dependency injection and HttpClient for API calls to the stubbed backend endpoints.\n- State Management:\n  - Keep selected engine family, categories, and parts in appropriate component or cascading state.\n  - Ensure part selections update UI instantly: use local state updates plus API calls as needed.\n- API Integration:\n  - Connect UI interactions to backend stubs:\n    - `POST /api/builds` from home “Create Build” button.\n    - `GET /api/builds/:id` when loading `BuilderPage`.\n    - `POST /api/builds/:id/selections` and `DELETE /api/builds/:id/selections` for selections updates.\n- Constraints:\n  - Work only within `app/` for code changes.\n  - Do not create `frontend/` or `backend/` subfolders.\n  - Do not break or refactor unrelated dashboard simulation features.\n\n---\n\n## Backend\n\n### Project Name\nRotary Builder MVP (EPIC 02)\n\n### Required Deliverables\n- Stubbed API Endpoints (in Blazor host / server or appropriate API project linked to `app/`):\n  - `POST /api/builds`\n    - Creates an in-memory build entity.\n    - Returns build ID and initial metrics.\n  - `GET /api/builds/:id`\n    - Returns build details for the given ID.\n  - `POST /api/builds/:id/selections`\n    - Accepts part selection changes and updates in-memory build data.\n    - Returns `{summary, completion, cost, warnings}`.\n  - `DELETE /api/builds/:id/selections`\n    - Clears or updates selections.\n    - Returns `{summary, completion, cost, warnings}`.\n- In-Memory Data Model:\n  - Structures to store:\n    - Builds (ID, engine family, selections).\n    - Part catalog (categories, parts, prices, required flags).\n  - Logic to compute:\n    - Completion % = (selected required parts / total required parts) * 100 (or defined rule).\n    - Total cost = sum of selected parts’ prices.\n    - Warnings = static + any selection-based logic.\n- Documentation:\n  - Update `docs/API.md`:\n    - Endpoint descriptions.\n    - Request/response examples with JSON payloads.\n  - Update `logs/CHANGELOG.md`:\n    - Summary line describing this Builder MVP implementation.\n\n### Key Technical Notes & Constraints\n- Implementation should align with the existing Blazor architecture:\n  - If there is a hosted ASP.NET Core backend, add controllers or minimal APIs for the routes under `/api/`.\n  - Ensure endpoints are reachable from the Blazor WebAssembly front-end.\n- In-Memory Only:\n  - No external database; store data in static or scoped in-memory collections.\n  - Keep it simple but deterministic enough for tests.\n- Response Schema:\n  - `summary`: short textual or structured overview of current build.\n  - `completion`: numeric value or object representing completion %.\n  - `cost`: numeric total.\n  - `warnings`: array/list of warning messages/objects.\n- Maintain compatibility:\n  - Do not alter or break existing dashboard endpoints or logic.\n  - Keep new logic isolated to builder-related namespaces/files where possible.\n\n---\n\n## Tester\n\n### Project Name\nRotary Builder MVP (EPIC 02)\n\n### Required Deliverables\n- Validation of all criteria in `TEST.md`:\n  - Mark or track pass/fail status for each test case.\n- Confirmed Documentation:\n  - Verify `README.md` has correct run instructions.\n  - Verify `docs/API.md` matches actual behavior.\n  - Verify `logs/CHANGELOG.md` contains a new summary line for this run.\n- Test Artifacts (optional but recommended):\n  - Notes or screenshots for critical flows (home page, builder page, error cases).\n\n### Key Technical Notes & Constraints\n- Environment Setup:\n  - Use `dotnet run` inside the `app/` directory to run the application.\n  - Test using supported browsers for Blazor WebAssembly (e.g., latest Chrome/Edge/Firefox).\n- Scope of Testing:\n  - Focus on:\n    - New Rotary Builder landing page and `/builder/{buildId}`.\n    - API correctness for the four new endpoints.\n    - Real-time UI updates for selections, completion, cost, warnings.\n  - Also confirm that existing dashboard simulation features are not regressed.\n- How to Test Endpoints:\n  - Use browser dev tools, `curl`, or a REST client (e.g., Postman) to inspect API traffic.\n  - Validate the presence and behavior of:\n    - `POST /api/builds`\n    - `GET /api/builds/:id`\n    - `POST /api/builds/:id/selections`\n    - `DELETE /api/builds/:id/selections`\n\ndesign/design_spec.md:\nRotary Builder MVP – UX / UI Design Spec\n=======================================\n\nProject Context\n---------------\nEPIC: EPIC 02 – Rotary Builder MVP  \nApp Type: Blazor WebAssembly (UI changes inside `app/` only)\n\nThis spec defines the UX, layout, and interaction patterns for:\n\n- Home (Rotary Builder landing) page – replaces existing home.\n- Builder page `/builder/{buildId}` – 3-column layout:\n  - Left: `CategoryTree`\n  - Center: `PartsList`\n  - Right: `SummaryRail` + `WarningsPanel`\n\nDesign Goals\n------------\n\n- Make “Create Build” the primary CTA on the home page.\n- Keep the UI simple, grid-based, and easy to map to Blazor components.\n- Provide “real-time-feeling” feedback (no full page reloads) when parts are selected.\n- Keep new styles scoped to builder components to avoid impacting existing dashboard areas.\n\nGlobal Visual Language (High-Level)\n-----------------------------------\n\n- Layout: Simple, responsive, single-page views with 12-column style mental model.\n- Colors / Typography:\n  - Reuse existing app base font and colors where possible (inherit from existing `app/wwwroot/` styles).\n  - Introduce new styles via classnames scoped to builder components (e.g., `.rb-...`) to avoid global overrides.\n- UI Density:\n  - Medium density: tabular center panel, simple list in left rail, compact cards on right rail.\n- Iconography:\n  - Optional, not required by MVP. Prefer text labels; add icons only if existing icon set is already in use.\n\n---\n\nHome Page – Rotary Builder Landing\n==================================\n\nRoute & Component Mapping\n-------------------------\n\n- File: `app/Pages/Index.razor` (or existing home page) becomes the Rotary Builder landing page.\n- It should function as a simple, focused “start screen” for builds.\n\nLayout Structure\n----------------\n\nVertical layout (top to bottom):\n\n1. **Header / Page Title**\n   - Text: “Rotary Builder” (or “Rotary Engine Builder”).\n   - Optional subtitle: Short description (e.g., “Configure a rotary engine build and see completion, cost, and warnings in real time.”).\n   - Left-aligned, with spacing below.\n\n2. **Engine Family Selector**\n   - Label: “Engine family”\n   - Control: Single-select dropdown (e.g., `<select>` or Blazor `InputSelect`).\n   - Options: A small static set (e.g., “13B”, “20B”, “12A”, “Other”) — exact list to be defined by implementation, doesn’t affect UX.\n   - Default behavior:\n     - Default selection can be “Select an engine family…” (placeholder) or a sensible default.\n     - If placeholder is used, “Create Build” should be disabled until a valid selection is chosen.\n   - Visual behavior:\n     - Standard input styling with clear focus/hover states following existing app conventions.\n\n3. **Primary Action Area**\n   - Primary button: “Create Build”\n   - Visual prominence:\n     - Solid, primary-colored button (use app’s existing primary button style).\n     - Placed near the engine family selector (same row on wide screens, stacked on narrow).\n   - Behavior:\n     - On click, triggers `POST /api/builds` with selected engine family.\n     - Disabled state:\n       - Disabled if:\n         - No engine family selected (if placeholder pattern used).\n         - A request is in-flight (to prevent double submit).\n     - Loading state:\n       - Optional small spinner / text change (e.g., “Creating…”).\n   - Secondary link or text (optional):\n     - Short helper text like “You’ll be taken to the builder to choose parts” below the button.\n\n4. **Informational Panel (Optional but Recommended)**\n   - Below the primary action, a light panel/card that explains:\n     - Step 1: Choose engine family & create a build.\n     - Step 2: Select parts by category.\n     - Step 3: Monitor completion, cost, and warnings.\n   - Purpose: Onboard internal stakeholders quickly.\n\nInteraction & Visual Behavior\n-----------------------------\n\n- **Create Build success**\n  - On success, navigate to `/builder/{buildId}` using the id returned from `POST /api/builds`.\n- **Create Build failure**\n  - Show a non-intrusive error message near the button or at the top of the panel (e.g., a red text line).\n  - Keep current selections; allow retry.\n- **Responsiveness**\n  - Desktop:\n    - Engine family dropdown and “Create Build” button can sit in one row: dropdown (left, wider) and button (right).\n  - Mobile / narrow width:\n    - Stack vertically: engine family selector, then button, each full-width.\n\n---\n\nBuilder Page – `/builder/{buildId}`\n===================================\n\nRoute & Component Mapping\n-------------------------\n\n- Page-level component:\n  - `app/Pages/BuilderPage.razor`\n  - Routed as `/builder/{buildId}` via Blazor routing.\n- Child components:\n  - `CategoryTree` – left rail navigation.\n  - `PartsList` – center content.\n  - `SummaryRail` – right metrics.\n  - `WarningsPanel` – right warnings list (stacked with SummaryRail).\n\nHigh-Level Layout\n-----------------\n\nThree-column responsive layout:\n\n- Left Rail: `CategoryTree` (fixed-ish width, e.g., 20–25% on desktop).\n- Center Panel: `PartsList` (flexible width, primary focus).\n- Right Rail: `SummaryRail` (top) + `WarningsPanel` (bottom), sized ~25–30% on desktop.\n\nOn desktop, layout is side-by-side:\n- [CategoryTree] | [PartsList] | [Summary + Warnings]\n\nOn mobile/tablet, collapse into vertical sections in this order:\n1. Summary + Warnings (so high-level status is visible first).\n2. CategoryTree (as a horizontal segment or toggleable section).\n3. PartsList.\n\nPage Header\n-----------\n\n- At the top of the builder page, above the three columns:\n  - Title: “Build #<id>” or “Rotary Build”.\n  - Secondary text: engine family name (if available from backend).\n  - Optional: A subtle “Status: In Progress” label.\n- Layout:\n  - Align left; use similar styling to landing page title but slightly smaller.\n\nLoading & Error States\n----------------------\n\n- Initial load (`GET /api/builds/:id`):\n  - Show a centered loader/spinner in the center panel, while a light grey skeleton or placeholder is shown for side rails.\n  - Hide parts list until data is ready.\n- Error (e.g., invalid build ID or API failure):\n  - Display an error banner at top of builder area:\n    - Example text: “Unable to load this build. Please check the URL or try again.”\n  - Optionally show a “Back to home” link.\n\n---\n\nLeft Rail – CategoryTree Component\n==================================\n\nPurpose\n-------\n\n- Display the static list/tree of 10 categories.\n- Allow user to switch between categories, which updates the `PartsList`.\n\nVisual Structure\n----------------\n\n- Container:\n  - A vertical panel with a title “Categories”.\n  - Light background or border to distinguish from center panel.\n- Category Items:\n  - 10 items total; flat list is acceptable for MVP.\n  - Each item shows:\n    - Category name (e.g., “Core”, “Intake”, “Exhaust”, etc. – names defined by implementation).\n    - Optional small indicator for completion in that category (recommended but not required):\n      - E.g., a small dot or check icon if all required parts for that category are selected.\n  - Text alignment: left.\n  - Visual spacing: 8–12px vertical padding between items.\n\nInteraction Behavior\n--------------------\n\n- Selection:\n  - Clicking a category sets it as the “active category”.\n  - The active category:\n    - Has a distinct visual style (e.g., highlight background, bold label, left border accent).\n- Hover / focus:\n  - Hover state (desktop): subtle background highlight.\n  - Focus outline (keyboard navigation) for accessibility.\n- Initial State:\n  - On first load, auto-select:\n    - The first category in the static list, or\n    - The last active category from build (if the API provides this – optional).\n- Scrolling:\n  - If the list height exceeds viewport height, the left rail should be scrollable vertically independent of the center panel.\n\nCommunication with Other Components\n-----------------------------------\n\n- `CategoryTree` notifies `BuilderPage` or shared state when:\n  - Active category changes.\n- `BuilderPage` passes to `PartsList`:\n  - The current selected category ID or key.\n\n---\n\nCenter Panel – PartsList Component\n==================================\n\nPurpose\n-------\n\n- Show parts available for the currently selected category.\n- Allow users to select / deselect parts.\n- Trigger recalculation of completion, cost, and warnings in real time.\n\nData & Layout\n-------------\n\n- Input data:\n  - Category identifier (current selection).\n  - Parts for that category (from static JSON or equivalent).\n  - Current build selections (to mark which parts are already chosen).\n- Visual structure:\n  - Panel header:\n    - Title: current category name.\n    - Optional count: “X parts available”.\n  - Main content:\n    - Tabular layout or card list.\n    - Suggested table columns:\n      - Part Name\n      - Description (short)\n      - Price\n      - Required (yes/no or indicator)\n      - Selection control (checkbox or radio, depending on part rules).\n    - Alternatively, cards if table styling is not available, but a table is preferred for clarity.\n\nSelection Controls\n------------------\n\n- Common Pattern:\n  - Use checkboxes for multi-select within category.\n  - If certain categories require exactly one selected (like “core type”), use radio buttons for that category.\n  - implementation can choose a simplified rule (e.g., all checkboxes) if business logic is not strict yet.\n- Visual cues:\n  - Selected row should be visually distinct:\n    - Slightly shaded background.\n    - Left border or check icon.\n  - Required parts:\n    - Indicator, e.g., “Required” badge or an asterisk near name.\n- Price:\n  - Right-aligned numeric values.\n  - Include currency symbol (e.g., “$1,200.00”) if consistent with existing app patterns.\n\nInteraction & API Behavior\n--------------------------\n\n- Selecting / Deselecting a Part:\n  - Immediate local UI update:\n    - Selection state (checkbox / radio) toggles instantly.\n    - Row styling reflects selection state.\n  - Then call appropriate endpoint:\n    - Add/update selection: `POST /api/builds/:id/selections`\n    - Remove selection: `DELETE /api/builds/:id/selections` (or reuse POST with appropriate payload – implementation choice).\n  - On response:\n    - Update:\n      - Completion percentage (SummaryRail).\n      - Total cost (SummaryRail).\n      - Warnings list (WarningsPanel).\n- Pending State:\n  - While an update call is in-flight:\n    - Option 1 (simple): keep UI interactive; handle last-write-wins behavior.\n    - Option 2 (safer): temporarily disable controls for the affected row, show a tiny inline spinner.\n  - Errors:\n    - If selection update fails:\n      - Revert the UI state for the affected part to its previous value.\n      - Show a small inline error message (e.g., “Couldn’t update selection. Try again.”) or a toast.\n\nEmpty / Edge States\n-------------------\n\n- No parts for category:\n  - Show a centered message: “No parts available for this category yet.”\n- No selections:\n  - All rows unselected; SummaryRail and WarningsPanel still visible but reflect empty state (e.g., 0% completion, $0.00 cost, “No warnings”).\n\n---\n\nRight Rail – SummaryRail & WarningsPanel\n========================================\n\nLayout\n------\n\n- Right rail container:\n  - Fixed-width-ish column with vertical stack:\n    1. SummaryRail (top)\n    2. WarningsPanel (bottom)\n  - Scroll behavior:\n    - If content exceeds viewport height, right rail can scroll independently OR allow page-level scrolling with right rail pinned at top.\n\nSummaryRail Component\n---------------------\n\nPurpose\n- Present key metrics:\n  - Completion percentage.\n  - Total cost.\n  - High-level summary text.\n\nVisual Structure\n- Container:\n  - Card-style box with border and small shadow (if consistent with app style).\n  - Title text: “Build Summary”.\n- Inside content:\n  1. **Completion**\n     - Label: “Completion”\n     - Value: “X% complete”\n     - Visual bar:\n       - Horizontal progress bar showing completion percentage (0–100%).\n       - Use a simple colored filled bar with a neutral background track.\n  2. **Total Cost**\n     - Label: “Total Cost”\n     - Value: `$X,XXX.XX`\n     - Emphasized with larger font than labels.\n  3. **Summary Text**\n     - Short, dynamic sentence, e.g.,\n       - “Selected 5 of 8 required parts.”\n       - “Engine family: 13B | 12 parts selected.”\n\nInteraction / Update Behavior\n- Updated whenever selection API returns new metrics:\n  - `completion`: updates the progress bar and displayed percentage.\n  - `cost`: updates the total cost figure.\n  - `summary`: updates the descriptive text.\n- Loading state:\n  - While waiting for initial `GET /api/builds/:id`:\n    - Show skeleton placeholders or “Loading summary…”.\n- Empty state:\n  - If no selections yet:\n    - completion: 0%\n    - cost: $0.00\n    - summary: e.g., “No parts selected yet. Start with a category on the left.”\n\nWarningsPanel Component\n-----------------------\n\nPurpose\n- Show warnings that reflect the current build’s state.\n\nVisual Structure\n- Container:\n  - Card-style box below SummaryRail.\n  - Title: “Warnings”.\n- Content:\n  - Warnings list:\n    - Each warning as a bullet or row:\n      - Icon or colored marker (optional) to indicate severity (e.g., warning vs info).\n      - Short warning message text (1–2 lines).\n  - Examples:\n    - “Critical: Required apex seals not selected.”\n    - “Info: You have selected multiple intake configurations.”\n\nInteraction / Update Behavior\n- Updates whenever the backend returns a new `warnings` list:\n  - From:\n    - Initial `GET /api/builds/:id`.\n    - Any `POST`/`DELETE` to `/api/builds/:id/selections`.\n- Empty state:\n  - If there are no warnings:\n    - Show low-key text: “No current warnings.” (or “All checks passed so far.”).\n- Long list:\n  - If warnings exceed a certain count (e.g., >5):\n    - Limit visible height and allow scroll within panel.\n    - Optionally show count in title: “Warnings (5)”.\n\nVisual Severity Cues (optional but recommended)\n- Color-coding:\n  - Critical / Error: red border or icon.\n  - Warning: amber.\n  - Info: neutral/blue.\n- If severity is not in API, assume single warning style (e.g., amber).\n\n---\n\nReal-Time State & Interaction Summary\n=====================================\n\nState Flow\n----------\n\n1. **Home Page**\n   - User picks engine family.\n   - User clicks “Create Build”.\n   - App calls `POST /api/builds` and navigates to `/builder/{buildId}` on success.\n\n2. **Builder Page Initial Load**\n   - On navigation to `/builder/{buildId}`:\n     - Call `GET /api/builds/:id` to fetch:\n       - Engine family\n       - Categories (or references)\n       - Parts and existing selections\n       - Initial summary, completion, cost, warnings.\n   - UI populates:\n     - Header: engine family & build label.\n     - CategoryTree: 10 static categories.\n     - PartsList: parts for default category.\n     - SummaryRail & WarningsPanel: metrics and warnings.\n\n3. **Part Selection / Deselection**\n   - User toggles selection in `PartsList`.\n   - UI immediately reflects the new selection state.\n   - App calls selection endpoint to update backend.\n   - On response:\n     - `SummaryRail` updates completion %, total cost, summary text.\n     - `WarningsPanel` updates warnings list.\n   - In case of error:\n     - Revert selection to previous state.\n     - Show inline or rail-level error message.\n\nVisual Behavior Notes (Specific Interactions)\n=============================================\n\nEngine Family Selector & “Create Build”\n---------------------------------------\n\n- Disabled “Create Build” when:\n  - No engine family selected (if using placeholder).\n  - A request is in progress.\n- If engine family changes while on home:\n  - It just updates local selection; no immediate API calls.\n- On click:\n  - Immediate feedback (button disabled or text changes).\n  - On success: transition to builder page without showing intermediate blank page (Blazor navigation).\n  - On failure: enable button again and show error text.\n\nCategory Selection\n------------------\n\n- Active category always clearly marked (highlight).\n- Switching categories:\n  - Updates `PartsList` to show the new category’s parts.\n  - Does *not* change current summary/warnings unless a selection changes.\n- Keyboard navigation:\n  - Up/Down arrow to move between categories (if possible in Blazor; recommended but not required).\n  - Enter/Space to activate a category.\n\nPart Selection\n--------------\n\n- Click row or the specific checkbox/radio:\n  - Toggling the control should:\n    - Change the row style instantly.\n    - Mark it as selected/unselected.\n- Hover state:\n  - Light highlight to indicate clickability.\n- Required but unselected parts:\n  - Could include a subtle “!” indicator or italic text in the row, but minimal for MVP.\n- If a part is disabled (e.g., due to incompatible combination; future enhancement):\n  - Greyed out, no hover highlight, tooltip explaining why – optional for MVP.\n\nSummary & Warnings Visibility\n-----------------------------\n\n- Right rail should always be visible (on desktop) while user scrolls through parts:\n  - Either:\n    - Entire builder area scrolls and right rail scrolls with it, or\n    - Right rail is sticky at top within viewport.\n- Warnings:\n  - For critical warnings, consider slightly stronger styling so they stand out, but avoid modal/popup.\n- No automatic scrolling:\n  - Selecting parts does not auto-scroll to warnings; they are visible in the right rail.\n\nResponsive Behavior\n===================\n\nDesktop (≥ ~1024px)\n--------------------\n\n- Layout: Three-column:\n  - Left rail: ~20–25%\n  - Center panel: ~45–55%\n  - Right rail: ~25–30%\n- Scrolling:\n  - Entire page scrollable, or independent scrolling columns where needed.\n\nTablet (~768–1023px)\n--------------------\n\n- Two-row layout for builder:\n  - Row 1: SummaryRail + WarningsPanel (full width or side-by-side).\n  - Row 2: CategoryTree (left) and PartsList (right) stacked or split:\n    - Option A: CategoryTree on top of PartsList (full width each).\n    - Option B: Reduced-width left rail beside a narrower PartsList.\n- Ensure tap targets are at least ~40px tall.\n\nMobile (< ~768px)\n-----------------\n\n- Single-column stack:\n  1. SummaryRail\n  2. WarningsPanel\n  3. CategoryTree\n  4. PartsList\n- CategoryTree:\n  - Could be collapsible/accordion labeled “Categories” to save vertical space.\n- PartsList:\n  - Table converts to card-like layout:\n    - Each part card shows:\n      - Name\n      - Price\n      - Required indicator\n      - Checkbox/radio\n      - Short description below.\n\nImplementation Alignment Notes\n==============================\n\n- Styles:\n  - Use CSS classes prefixed (for example) with `rb-` to scope new styles:\n    - `.rb-builder-layout`, `.rb-category-rail`, `.rb-parts-list`, `.rb-summary-rail`, `.rb-warnings-panel`.\n  - Add new CSS in a way that doesn’t override global `body`, `table`, etc., unless coordinated with existing styles.\n- Components:\n  - `BuilderPage.razor`:\n    - Responsible for:\n      - Route.\n      - Data fetching for build.\n      - Providing data/state to child components.\n  - `CategoryTree.razor`:\n    - Purely presentational for categories; raises events on selection change.\n  - `PartsList.razor`:\n    - Presentational + interaction for parts.\n    - Emits events for part selection changes.\n  - `SummaryRail.razor` & `WarningsPanel.razor`:\n    - Stateless UI bound to props/parameters for summary, completion, cost, warnings.\n\nAcceptance-Impacting UX Clarifications\n======================================\n\n- Completion calculation:\n  - UX expects a single numeric percentage (0–100) and a short summary line.\n  - Visual progress bar and label must update on every selection change.\n- Warnings:\n  - List must visually change when parts are added or removed if backend updates warnings.\n- No blocking modals:\n  - Errors should be inline (message near where they occur) and must not block all interactions.\n\nThis spec should provide enough detail for the frontend and backend implementers to map endpoints, state, and component structure into a coherent, testable UI without modifying unrelated dashboard features.\n\nBlazor Guardrails:\n- ONLY write files under app/.\n- Do NOT write to frontend/.\n- Update app/Pages/* and app/wwwroot/* for UI.\n\n'}]}], 'instructions': '# System context\nYou are part of a multi-agent system called the Agents SDK, designed to make agent coordination and execution easy. The builder lets users configure a rotary engine build by selecting parts, viewing completion, cost, and warnings in real time.\n\n## Target Users\n- Internal team members and stakeholders evaluating the Rotary Builder concept.\n- Future end-users (e.g., engine builders/enthusiasts) as early prototype users.\n\n## In-Scope\n- Blazor WebAssembly app changes inside `app/` only.\n- Frontend UI:\n  - New Rotary Builder landing page as the home page.\n  - Dedicated builder page at `/builder/{buildId}`.\n  - Real-time UI state updates when selecting/deselecting parts.\n- Backend (stubbed, in-memory only):\n  - Build creation and retrieval.\n  - Managing part selections for a build.\n  - Returning computed metrics (summary, completion, cost, warnings).\n- Documentation:\n  - Update `docs/API.md` with example payloads for each new endpoint.\n  - Update `logs/CHANGELOG.md` with a summary line for this run.\n  - Add root-level `README.md` with setup and run instructions.\n- Data:\n  - Static category tree (10 categories).\n  - Static parts JSON for each category.\n  - Static warnings list is acceptable for MVP, but must update based on selection actions where appropriate.\n\n## Out of Scope / Constraints\n- NO authentication.\n- NO scraping.\n- NO 3D rendering.\n- Do not modify unrelated dashboard simulation features.\n- Do not create new `frontend/` or `backend/` folders.\n- Work only inside the existing `app/` folder for the Blazor app implementation.\n- Project structure constraints:\n  - Use and update existing Blazor files such as:\n    - `app/Program.cs`\n    - `app/Pages/*`\n    - `app/wwwroot/*`\n- Must support running the Blazor app locally via `dotnet run` in `app/`.\n\n## Key Features\n\n### 1. Rotary Builder Landing (Home Page)\n- The app’s home page becomes the Rotary Builder landing page.\n- Displays:\n  - Engine family selector (basic dropdown or similar control).\n  - A prominent “Create Build” action.\n- Behavior:\n  - Clicking “Create Build” calls `POST /api/builds`.\n  - On success, navigates to `/builder/{buildId}`.\n\n### 2. Builder Page: `/builder/{buildId}`\nMain layout:\n- Left rail: CategoryTree\n  - Shows 10 categories in a tree or flat list (static seeded list acceptable).\n  - Selecting a category updates the center panel.\n- Center panel: PartsList\n  - Lists parts for the selected category from static JSON.\n  - Allows selecting/deselecting parts.\n- Right rail: SummaryRail + WarningsPanel\n  - Displays:\n    - Completion percentage (selected vs required parts).\n    - Total build cost (sum of selected part prices).\n    - Warnings list (static examples OK, but must respond to write actions data).\n\n### 3. Real-time State Updates\n- Selecting/deselecting parts:\n  - Updates completion %, total cost, and warnings immediately without full page refresh.\n  - Uses Blazor component state and/or API calls to stub endpoints.\n- Write actions (selection changes) must return:\n  - `{ summary, completion, cost, warnings }` (shape to be defined in API docs).\n\n### 4. Backend Stub Endpoints\nStubbed, in-memory storage only (no external DB):\n\n- `POST /api/builds`\n  - Creates a new build with default state.\n  - Returns build ID and initial summary/metrics.\n- `GET /api/builds/:id`\n  - Returns build details including:\n    - Engine family.\n    - Selected parts.\n    - Available categories/parts (or references to static lists).\n    - Summary, completion, cost, warnings.\n- `POST /api/builds/:id/selections`\n  - Accepts selection changes for parts (e.g., add/update).\n  - Recomputes completion, cost, warnings.\n  - Returns `{ summary, completion, cost, warnings }`.\n- `DELETE /api/builds/:id/selections`\n  - Accepts info to remove/reset selections.\n  - Recomputes metrics.\n  - Returns `{ summary, completion, cost, warnings }`.\n\n## Non-Functional Requirements\n- Local development:\n  - Clear instructions in root `README.md` for:\n    - Installing prerequisites.\n    - Running via `dotnet run` inside `app/`.\n- Performance:\n  - Real-time feeling for part selection updates (no full-page reloads).\n  - Reasonable responsiveness for UI state changes with in-memory data.\n- Code Quality:\n  - Clean separation of components:\n    - `BuilderPage`\n    - `CategoryTree`\n    - `PartsList`\n    - `SummaryRail`\n    - `WarningsPanel`\n  - Do not break or refactor unrelated dashboard functionality.\n- Testing:\n  - Define clear acceptance criteria and manual test steps in `TEST.md`.\n  - Tester should be able to validate all acceptance criteria using the documented steps.\n\n---\n\nAGENT_TASKS.md:\n# EPIC 02: Builder MVP – Agent Tasks\n\n---\n\n## Designer\n\n### Project Name\nRotary Builder MVP (EPIC 02)\n\n### Required Deliverables\n- `README.md` (root)\n  - `GET /api/builds/:id` when loading `BuilderPage`.\n    - `POST /api/builds/:id/selections` and `DELETE /api/builds/:id/selections` for selections updates.\n- Constraints:\n  - Work only within `app/` for code changes.\n  - Do not create `frontend/` or `backend/` subfolders.\n  - Do not break or refactor unrelated dashboard simulation features.\n\n---\n\n## Backend\n\n### Project Name\nRotary Builder MVP (EPIC 02)\n\n### Required Deliverables\n- Stubbed API Endpoints (in Blazor host / server or appropriate API project linked to `app/`):\n  - `POST /api/builds`\n    - Creates an in-memory build entity.\n    - Returns build ID and initial metrics.\n  - `GET /api/builds/:id`\n    - Returns build details for the given ID.\n  - `POST /api/builds/:id/selections`\n    - Accepts part selection changes and updates in-memory build data.\n    - Returns `{summary, completion, cost, warnings}`.\n  - `DELETE /api/builds/:id/selections`\n    - Clears or updates selections.\n    - Returns `{summary, completion, cost, warnings}`.\n- In-Memory Data Model:\n  - Structures to store:\n    - Builds (ID, engine family, selections).\n    - Part catalog (categories, parts, prices, required flags).\n  - Logic to compute:\n    - Completion % = (selected required parts / total required parts) * 100 (or defined rule).\n    - Total cost = sum of selected parts’ prices.\n    - Warnings = static + any selection-based logic.\n- Documentation:\n  - Update `docs/API.md`:\n    - Endpoint descriptions.\n    - Request/response examples with JSON payloads.\n  - Update `logs/CHANGELOG.md`:\n    - Summary line describing this Builder MVP implementation.\n\n### Key Technical Notes & Constraints\n- Implementation should align with the existing Blazor architecture:\n  - If there is a hosted ASP.NET Core backend, add controllers or minimal APIs for the routes under `/api/`.\n  - Ensure endpoints are reachable from the Blazor WebAssembly front-end.\n- In-Memory Only:\n  - No external database; store data in static or scoped in-memory collections.\n  - Keep it simple but deterministic enough for tests.\n- Response Schema:\n  - `summary`: short textual or structured overview of current build.\n  - `completion`: numeric value or object representing completion %.\n  - `cost`: numeric total.\n  - `warnings`: array/list of warning messages/objects.\n- Maintain compatibility:\n  - Do not alter or break existing dashboard endpoints or logic.\n  - Keep new logic isolated to builder-related namespaces/files where possible.\n\n---\n\n## Tester\n\n### Project Name\nRotary Builder MVP (EPIC 02)\n\n### Required Deliverables\n- Validation of all criteria in `TEST.md`:\n  - Home Page Becomes Rotary Builder Landing\n\n### 1.1 Home page layout and content\n- [Designer][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1. Run the app (`dotnet run` in `app/`).\n  2. Open the app root URL in a browser.\n- Acceptance Criteria:\n  - The initial page is clearly a “Rotary Builder” landing page.\n  - The page contains an “Engine family” selector (dropdown or equivalent).\n  - There is a prominent “Create Build” button or CTA.\n  - No previous dashboard-only landing page is visible or conflicting.\n\n### 1.2 Create Build navigation behavior\n- [Frontend][Backend][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1. On the landing page, choose an engine family (if required).\n  2. Click “Create Build”.\n- Acceptance Criteria:\n  - A `POST /api/builds` request is sent.\n  - The app navigates to `/builder/{buildId}` where `buildId` is the ID returned by the API.\n  - No full browser refresh is required for navigation (Blazor routing).\n\n---\n\n## 2. Builder Page Routing: `/builder/{buildId}`\n\n### 2.1 Route configuration and rendering\n- [Frontend][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1. Manually navigate to `/builder/test-id` in the browser (after app is running).\n- Acceptance Criteria:\n  - The URL `/builder/{buildId}` is recognized by Blazor routing.\n  - `BuilderPage` component is rendered without runtime errors.\n  - If `buildId` is invalid, the UI displays an appropriate error or “build not found” message.\n\n### 2.2 Loading initial build data\n- [Frontend][Backend][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1. Create a build via the landing page.\n  2. Confirm that `/builder/{buildId}` loads initial build data.\n- Acceptance Criteria:\n  - `GET /api/builds/:id` is called when `BuilderPage` loads.\n  - The UI shows initial selections, completion %, cost, and warnings consistent with stubbed data.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Left Rail Category Tree (10 Categories)\n\n### 3.1 Category tree presence and count\n- [Designer][Frontend][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1. On `/builder/{buildId}`, inspect the left rail.\n- Acceptance Criteria:\n  - There is a clearly defined CategoryTree component or equivalent.\n  - Exactly 10 categories are visible (static seeded list is acceptable).\n  - Category labels are readable and visually distinct as a list or tree.\n  - Selecting a category indicates active state (highlight, selected styling, or similar).\n\n### 3.2 Category selection behavior\n- [Frontend][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1. Click on multiple different categories in the left rail.\n- Acceptance Criteria:\n  - The active category state visually updates as categories are clicked.\n  - The center panel’s parts list updates to show the selected category’s parts.\n  - No full page reload occurs.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Center Panel PartsList\n\n### 4.1 Static parts data display\n- [Frontend][Backend][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1. With various categories selected, inspect the center panel.\n- Acceptance Criteria:\n  - The PartsList component renders parts for the active category.\n  - Data is sourced from static JSON or static in-memory data (as implemented).\n  - Each part displays at least:\n    - Name\n    - Price\n    - Any selection control (checkbox, radio, button, etc.).\n\n### 4.2 Part selection/deselection\n- [Frontend][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1. For multiple parts in the visible list, toggle their selection status.\n- Acceptance Criteria:\n  - UI clearly shows selected vs unselected states per part.\n  - Selected parts remain selected when interacting with other UI regions.\n  - Selections survive simple UI re-render events (e.g., changing category and returning, if supported by data model).\n\n---\n\n## 5. Right Rail: SummaryRail and WarningsPanel\n\n### 5.1 Summary metrics display\n- [Designer][Frontend][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1. On the builder page, inspect the right rail.\n- Acceptance Criteria:\n  - SummaryRail shows:\n    - Completion percentage.\n    - Total cost of the build.\n  - WarningsPanel shows a list of warnings (can be static examples at first).\n  - Layout is visually coherent with clear labels.\n\n### 5.2 Metric and warnings behavior on selection changes\n- [Frontend][Backend][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1. Select and deselect parts across one or more categories.\n  2. Observe right rail metrics.\n- Acceptance Criteria:\n  - Completion percentage updates immediately after part selection changes.\n  - Total cost updates immediately based on selected parts’ prices.\n  - Warnings list updates in response to selection changes where implemented, or otherwise remains consistent with stubbed logic.\n  - No full page reload occurs during these updates.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Real-time Updates & API Contracts\n\n### 6.1 UI updates without full refresh\n- [Frontend][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1. Perform several rapid part selections and deselections.\n- Acceptance Criteria:\n  - UI remains responsive.\n  - No browser-level full page reloads occur.\n  - Only relevant components re-render (Blazor behavior).\n\n### 6.2 Write actions response shape\n- [Backend][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1. Using browser dev tools or a REST client, call:\n     - `POST /api/builds/:id/selections`\n     - `DELETE /api/builds/:id/selections`\n  2. Make valid payload requests according to `docs/API.md`.\n- Acceptance Criteria:\n  - Both endpoints respond with a JSON object containing:\n    - `summary`\n    - `completion`\n    - `cost`\n    - `warnings`\n  - Fields are present and data types are consistent with API documentation.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Backend Stub Endpoints\n\n### 7.1 POST /api/builds\n- [Backend][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1. Send `POST /api/builds` without body or with minimal required payload (per docs).\n- Acceptance Criteria:\n  - Endpoint returns HTTP 200 or 201 (as designed).\n  - Response includes:\n    - A unique `id` (buildId).\n    - Initial summary/metrics consistent with defaults.\n  - In-memory structures allow subsequent `GET /api/builds/:id`.\n\n### 7.2 GET /api/builds/:id\n- [Backend][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1. Create a build.\n  2. Call `GET /api/builds/{id}`.\n- Acceptance Criteria:\n  - Endpoint returns HTTP 200 for valid ID.\n  - Payload includes:\n    - Engine family.\n    - Current selected parts.\n    - Completion percentage, cost, warnings.\n  - Returns 404 or clear error for unknown build ID.\n\n### 7.3 POST /api/builds/:id/selections\n- [Backend][Tester]\n- Steps:\n  1.
